  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_c0456e62-b9ca-4793-9b48-b7f811472780'
      });

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer6797522836028333803">Oliver Marks has just served ten years in jail - for a murder he may or may not have committed. On the day he's released, he's greeted by the man who put him in prison. Detective Colborne is retiring, but before he does, he wants to know what really happened a decade ago.<br/><br/>As one of seven young actors studying Shakespeare at an elite arts college, Oliver and his friends play</span>
  <span id="freeText6797522836028333803" style="display:none">Oliver Marks has just served ten years in jail - for a murder he may or may not have committed. On the day he's released, he's greeted by the man who put him in prison. Detective Colborne is retiring, but before he does, he wants to know what really happened a decade ago.<br /><br />As one of seven young actors studying Shakespeare at an elite arts college, Oliver and his friends play the same roles onstage and off: hero, villain, tyrant, temptress, ingenue, extra. But when the casting changes, and the secondary characters usurp the stars, the plays spill dangerously over into life, and one of them is found dead. The rest face their greatest acting challenge yet: convincing the police, and themselves, that they are blameless.</span>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    I would say yes because of Pericles, which is what James leaves a passage of in his note to Oliver. Pericles believes his wife to have drowned at sea <a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    I would say yes because of Pericles, which is what James leaves a passage of in his note to Oliver. Pericles believes his wife to have drowned at sea and after asking for help (which Oliver mentions) finds her alive in a religious temple.<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/66937166-jerlin-rajan"><img alt="" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_100x100-259587f1619f5253426a4fa6fb508831.png" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/66937166-jerlin-rajan">Jerlin Rajan</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    I do think that he loved Oliver but not as much as Oliver to James, it's annoying to say that James was manipulating, being the upper hand, being the <a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    I do think that he loved Oliver but not as much as Oliver to James, it's annoying to say that James was manipulating, being the upper hand, being the puppet master to Oliver's strings. Oliver being 'naive' and oblivious, he was so in love, he missed the signs. He realised he was an easy target and hooked Oliver into his own game that he didn't even he was playing. James is similar to Richard, dark, deep and rich in mind games. James felt guilty yes he made it sure, he felt that way but tell me something, if you felt guilty if you were in Jame's situation so badly what would you do? I will tell the detective I have done it. It's my mistake, I wouldn't want someone else taking the blame that's going to affect their future. James was just stringing easy there saying 'can I do anything to help' he knows what he did and he left a passage to Oliver saying he could be alive. Now that shows us, he's alive and he needs Oliver to be next to him, to pay back the times James took away which is (hope, despair, himself) from Oliver. Oliver showed us that he is the bigger man metaphorically. He used Oliver by using the 'i love you, Oliver, please take it for me' card although not intentionally. He could have easily told him at the start and let him go to Jail. James didn't want to tell him because he would be disappointing him and he doesn't want to do that to the one he loves. So honestly, I think James loved him when he went to Jail for him, he could have realised what he did for him, risking his life for him. James could have wanted to give his life to Oliver. <a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</span>
</div>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div id="review_2172798816" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2172798816" />
    <a title="chai ♡" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42130592-chai"><img alt="chai ♡" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603167303p2/42130592.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2172798816?book_show_action=true">Oct 09, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="chai ♡" class="user" itemprop="url" name="chai ♡" href="/user/show/42130592-chai">chai ♡</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=adult-thriller-mystery">adult-thriller-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=trope-friends-to-lovers">trope-friends-to-lovers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=trope-omg-they-were-roommates">trope-omg-they-were-roommates</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=adult-contemporary">adult-contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=trope-gay-yearning">trope-gay-yearning</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=trope-doomed-tragic-love">trope-doomed-tragic-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=trope-idiots-in-love">trope-idiots-in-love</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2172798816" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4312606230346459560">Folks, when you come across this book, you’ll hear a voice saying, “Oh, this sounds interesting! Do it.” <strong>That’s the devil talking.</strong><br/><br/>I hate this book so much I can't bear it. I tore through it, but I feel like it tore through <em>me</em>. That ending grabbed an invisible dagger and twisted it between my ribs. I didn’t want to talk for like...three years. I was exhausted. My heart felt like it was rammed by a semi-truck.<br/><br/>Fuck you, book. You're a bound bundle of dead tree. How dare you.<br/><br/><strong>
  <u>So, what’s this book </u></strong></span>
  <span id="freeText4312606230346459560" style="display:none">Folks, when you come across this book, you’ll hear a voice saying, “Oh, this sounds interesting! Do it.” <strong>That’s the devil talking.</strong><br /><br />I hate this book so much I can't bear it. I tore through it, but I feel like it tore through <em>me</em>. That ending grabbed an invisible dagger and twisted it between my ribs. I didn’t want to talk for like...three years. I was exhausted. My heart felt like it was rammed by a semi-truck.<br /><br />Fuck you, book. You're a bound bundle of dead tree. How dare you.<br /><br /><strong>
  <u>So, what’s this book about?</u>
</strong><br /><br /><em>If We Were Villains</em> spans multiple years and characters, but it zooms in on a tightly knit group of seven lyric-mad Shakespearean thespians who seemed to prefer each other’s company to anyone else’s, thereby offending the rest of the world. But at some point, something dark had sown hatred in them and wedged its way between them, and that friendship, once beautiful, later held something worth fearing. At some point, they’d become less friends and more things for each other to hit.<br /><br />Then, almost inevitably, <strong>a murder</strong>.<br /><br />Now, ten years later, detective Colborne feels every choice he’d made, every action he’d taken that fatal night, as a weight he carried with him. There were so many versions of the story everyone had made up—neat distillations of what had happened.<br /><br />Only one person can say which one was true.<br /><br />The secrets Oliver Marks had kept had sharp edges. Now, no longer prison-bound, with the realization that there was no darkness Colborne could send him to rival what he’d endured already, Oliver is ready to put the last spectre of the past where it belongs, his brain going there, dredging up those years again, churning them to the surface to be rewound and replayed, remembering…<br /><br />The truth surging back with a vengeance.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>“Do you blame Shakespeare for any of it?” </em>
  <br />
  <em>The question is so unlikely, so nonsensical coming from such a sensible man, that I can’t suppress a smile. “I blame him for all of it,” I say.</em>
</blockquote><br /><br />I am still so deeply struck by the elegance of a story that appealed to my dark academia loving heart on such a profound spiritual level. Shakespearian aesthetics, higher learning, homoeroticism, a secret society that exists vaguely where everyone communicates with pretentious quotes, characters doing morally grey things at odd hours, a devastating murder, and M.L. Rio has set the scene for <strong>an exhilarating, unsettling and invigoratingly taut thriller</strong>. It was almost inevitable for me to be hopelessly flummoxed well before the halfway point.<br /><br />The intricate plot turnings, the meticulous character work and the staggering revelations of the narration made this book <strong>a real page-turner</strong>. The kind of book you initially think you can read in quick bursts and clashes but which ends up sucking you in for hours at a time. I constantly fell into the lie that I’d read <em>just one more page</em>, and as a result, I missed class. I even missed lunch. And when I finally finished it, I was so obsessed I literally almost flipped back to the beginning to start again!<br /><br />I am still reeling with shocks. This book was shock upon shock and I couldn’t shake the horrible feeling all the players were stepping onto the stage, but no one had ever bothered to give me a script. Everything I'd wondered about the characters took on a much darker cast than I could ever have imagined. I was still grasping at the small things I hoped might tell a different story when the ending happened. And <em>oh my god</em>. There was a moment where I stopped everything, and my heart flew to my throat in disbelief at what Rio had just done. There was just no way to make my mind accept the possibility of it, because as terrible as imagining what happened might be, it has to be better than living in this current reality of <em>not-knowing</em>.<br /><br />Seriously. Who, with all due respect, <em>the fuck</em> allowed that ending?<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>“But that is how a tragedy like ours or King Lear breaks your heart—by making you believe that the ending might still be happy, until the very last minute.”</em>
</blockquote><br /><br />It’s also hard not to fall as instantly in love with each of these characters, with the encompassing attraction of a group of friends who have made ruins of each other, with the intoxicating chemistry between two lovers who held each other in plain sight of the world, though their bodies remained forever separate. It’s impossible not to feel caught up in the pull of everything—the thorny tangle of guilt, frustration, and longing, the rivalry, the blurred lines between love and hate, the fractured loyalties and determined single-minded violent obsessions that can never end well for most, but make a spellbinding story for the ones who survive to tell.<br /><br />I mean, sure, if you frame this book in the context of real life, it’s like, “wow, if I knew someone this pretentious in person, I wouldn’t hesitate to smack them upside the head.” But this is fiction and the way I feel about these characters is Steve Harrington going from a popular teenage boy to an extremely stressed-out single soccer mom with four kids in the span of a few days. They're literally all different shades of horrible and undoubtedly morally compromised but I'm still willing to lay down my kidneys for all of them. (Except Richard. He really did live up to the abbreviation of his name.)<br /><br />In conclusion, if reading <em>If We Were Villains</em> doesn’t make you want to get with a very tight-knit group of morally questionable Shakespeare devotees with an unhealthy obsession with aesthetics, and together you try to cover up a murder one of you committed, then who even are you?<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>Actors are by nature volatile—alchemic creatures composed of incendiary elements, emotion and ego and envy. Heat them up, stir them together, and sometimes you get gold. Sometimes disaster.</em>
</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>☆ <a href="https://ko-fi.com/givemeabrekk" rel="nofollow noopener">ko-fi</a> ★ <a href="https://bookswithchaima.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">blog</a> ☆ <a href="https://twitter.com/givemeabrekk" rel="nofollow noopener">twitter</a> ★ <a href="https://azqaban.tumblr.com" rel="nofollow noopener">tumblr</a> ☆<br /><br /><u>❗️<strong>SPOILERY SECTION</strong>❗️</u><br /><br />I know everyone who’s read this book is having a hard time right now and I’m here to say: what the FUCK.<br /><br />I love Oliver and James SO MUCH and they deserved so much more time together, more than a fleeting kiss shared on a Shakespeare scene before one of them is whisked away to a ten-years prison sentence because he took the fall for the man he loves (the only romantic gesture). Oliver didn’t even get to realize that he was actually in love with James while they were together. It had to happen while they were apart. Also, imagine thinking for six fucking years that the love of your life has given up on you and moved on because they no longer visit you, when in reality they’ve… FAKED their death. Speaking of which, if anyone tries to pry away from me the fact that James is somewhere waiting for Oliver to find him, it could only be my cold, dead hands, and you’d catch these hands from the grave. I REFUSE to believe otherwise.<br /><br />Anyway, If We Were Villains takes a Shakespearean tragedy to a whole new level. Eat your heart out, Shakespeare.<br /><br />ALSO, please read this fanfic because it's the ending we all deserved. It might not be canon but it's canon in MY HEART: <strong><a href="https://archiveofourown.org/works/15406506" rel="nofollow noopener">what is woven into the lives of others </a>by </strong>helloearthlings.</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="4312606230346459560" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2526253759" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7300885907595282658">reread and its good to know that dark academia is still my aesthetic and this story still owns my heart and soul. <br/><br/>____________________________________<br/><br/>this book! this book! my kingdom for this book!<br/><br/>this is absolutely sensational, a true work of brilliance. i am so enamoured by this story and everything it has to offer. its quite clever and beyond invigorating - the type of book that fully immerses you whilst reading it. <br/><br/>the passion which radiates throughout this story makes me feel so in love wit</span>
  <span id="freeText7300885907595282658" style="display:none">reread and its good to know that dark academia is still my aesthetic and this story still owns my heart and soul. <br /><br />____________________________________<br /><br />this book! this book! my kingdom for this book!<br /><br />this is absolutely sensational, a true work of brilliance. i am so enamoured by this story and everything it has to offer. its quite clever and beyond invigorating - the type of book that fully immerses you whilst reading it. <br /><br />the passion which radiates throughout this story makes me feel so in love with shakespeare and his words (and i honestly never considered myself a fan). the way in which these students dedicate their lives to studying him is almost romantic, in a way. how they integrate his language into their own interactions, making their own lives a work of poetry in the process, is very inspiring. <br /><br />and because of that, i would say the characters are the main focus for me. yes, there is a mystery/thriller element that surrounds the students, but i feel like that takes a backseat to what are phenomenal characters, the boys in particular. i became so enthralled with their lives, how they orbited one another, and just their day-to-day routines. <br /><br />and i should have known not to get so attached, as this story follows the form of a true shakespearean tragedy. so as i closed the final page, i found myself wistfully thinking that parting is such sweet sorrow.<br /><br /><b>↠ <i>5 stars</i></b></span>

<div id="review_2017885442" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2017885442" />
    <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines"><img alt="Elle (ellexamines)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582250895p2/52545435.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2017885442?book_show_action=true">Nov 22, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elle (ellexamines)" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines">Elle (ellexamines)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781250095299" href="/book/show/34275217-if-we-were-villains">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Elle by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/40511295-aleksandra">Aleksandra</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=elle-recs-list">elle-recs-list</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=identity">identity</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-faves2019">z-faves2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=plot-twists">plot-twists</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=y-out2017">y-out2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=mystery-suspense">mystery-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=favorite-characters">favorite-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=gay-genre-fiction">gay-genre-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=villain-antihero-arcs">villain-antihero-arcs</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2017885442" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4602399230187351655"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>You can justify anything, if you do it poetically enough.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>this is going to be one of my favorite books of the year... almost definitely. I’m saying that now on January 26th because I want you all to know. I genuinely cannot remember the last time I found myself so utterly engaged in a book. <br/><br/>Okay, so this is a drama set at a Shakespeare theater, in which a group of theater actors accidentally kill a man and deal with the fallout. Yay! Fun happy stuff. As the plays continue, their roles</span>
  <span id="freeText4602399230187351655" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>You can justify anything, if you do it poetically enough.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />this is going to be one of my favorite books of the year... almost definitely. I’m saying that now on January 26th because I want you all to know. I genuinely cannot remember the last time I found myself so utterly engaged in a book. <br /><br />Okay, so this is a drama set at a Shakespeare theater, in which a group of theater actors accidentally kill a man and deal with the fallout. Yay! Fun happy stuff. As the plays continue, their roles within this drama shift and switch, ironically mirroring their respective development, and they accidentally get <i>way</i> too involved in several plays as they are occuring. <br /><br />Dark academia is actually such a compelling and amazing genre to me, always, but Shakespearean drama is perhaps the <i>best</i> dark academia pick out there. We have moral intrigue!! long soliloquys!! everyone knows who he is, but he still has plenty of speeches no one knows!! gay subtext used to its best degree!! <br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>We cracked up. But we didn't really shatter until we came back together again.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />The seven lead characters each fit into well-known archetypes:<br />→Oliver - the lacking-type boy.<br />→James - the good guy. <br />→Alexander - the villain.<br />→Meredith - the sexpot. <br />→Wren - the ingenue. <br />→Phillipa - the lacking-type girl. bi. I have no proof but definitely bi. <br />→Richard - the dick himself. <br /><br />The degree to which the character dynamics affect this plot is just so so amazing. There is a genuine actual love triangle, as in every branch has some weird tension. (Actually, I don’t know how to make a love dynamic of this friend circle. Help them.)<br /><br />I don’t really know how to describe what made this book <b>so completely enthralling</b>. This isn’t a book focused on plot twists; I figured out most of the plot points here, actually, aside from a couple mini reveals. Yet every plot point, whether guessed or not, is satisfying, placed perfectly and used perfectly. This is a Shakespearean tragedy and on some level, we know how it ends. But <b>it is completely impossible to get off the tracks.</b><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“But that is how a tragedy like ours or King Lear breaks your heart—by making you believe that the ending might still be happy, until the very last minute.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />And you know what, this book would have been a five no matter how it ended, but the ending made me screech out loud. So there’s that. <br /><br />I want to thank <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2172798816?book_show_action=true" rel="nofollow noopener">Chaima</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2532335601?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Melanie</a>, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/40511295-aleksandra" rel="nofollow noopener"> Aleksandra </a>for encouraging me to read this, because honestly... dear god.<br /><br /><a href="https://thebookishactress.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/thebookishactress" rel="nofollow noopener">Goodreads</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/jespergayhey" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/thebookishactress/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="http://www.youtube.com/c/thebookishactress" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="4602399230187351655" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2749956066" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2749956066" />
    <a title=" Teodora " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69603149-teodora"><img alt=" Teodora " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582144281p2/69603149.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2749956066?book_show_action=true">May 17, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Teodora " class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Teodora " href="/user/show/69603149-teodora"> Teodora </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69603149-teodora?shelf=on-app">on-app</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69603149-teodora?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69603149-teodora?shelf=mystery-thriller">mystery-thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2749956066" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15913266500595153851">5/5 ⭐<br/><br/><b>Full review on my Blog:</b> <a href='https://thedacianshewolf.home.blog/2020/07/21/if-we-were-villains-by-m-l-rio/' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Dacian She-Wolf</a> 🐺<br/><blockquote>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1588085978i/29370765._SY540_.jpg' width='280' height='361' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
  <br/>
  <br/>
  <i>
    <b>“We felt all the passions of the characters we played as if they were our own. But a character’s emotions don’t cancel out the actor’s – instead you feel both at once.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/>I can’t even express how <b>upset</b> I am to see how <b>underrated</b> this book is. Like, how the fuck??<br/><br/>This is such a good book; I’ve been obsessed with it for at least a week straight and even though I felt the urge to devour it, I didn’t want it to end so fast so I had </span>
  <span id="freeText15913266500595153851" style="display:none">5/5 ⭐<br><br><b>Full review on my Blog:</b> <a href="https://thedacianshewolf.home.blog/2020/07/21/if-we-were-villains-by-m-l-rio/" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dacian She-Wolf</a> 🐺<br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1588085978i/29370765._SY540_.jpg" width="280" height="361" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  <br>
  <br>
  <i>
    <b>“We felt all the passions of the characters we played as if they were our own. But a character’s emotions don’t cancel out the actor’s – instead you feel both at once.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br>I can’t even express how <b>upset</b> I am to see how <b>underrated</b> this book is. Like, how the fuck??<br><br>This is such a good book; I’ve been obsessed with it for at least a week straight and even though I felt the urge to devour it, I didn’t want it to end so fast so I had to slow down and enjoy. You know what happened when I did that? <b>I truly enjoyed it.</b><br><br><i>
  <b>If We Were Villains</b>
</i> is part of this dark academia aesthetics that has a soothing place in my heart. So, of course, I fell in love with it. <br>I mean, how couldn’t I? I am a natural-born drama queen, I feed on theatrical stuff like this, do you expect me not to fell in love with a bunch of college kids aspiring to become actors?<br><br>You are terrible wrong if your answer was <i>yes</i>. Because I delight in drama. <i>(Telenovelas might have a say to that but uhm, who can say for sure?)</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1492279045ra/22501674.gif" width="361" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This book is a mystery-crime story and it debuts in the life of seven theatre students after one of them dies (quite tragically).<br><br>I honestly can feel the pertinence of this group. They really look like real-life people whom you might get acquainted with at some point in life. I love their dynamics as a group, but I have different feelings for each of them.<br><br>- <b>Oliver</b> is one of my favourites and, it seems, the protagonist of the book; he’s always the sidekick, always the nice guy with a good heart; always loyal; he could do anything for those whom he loves; and he does; <i>how could one not love him?</i><br>- <b>James</b> is another favourite of mine; he’s always the good guy, the hero, the one with a noble heart; he’s definitely a Prince Charming and honestly, my heart just melts for him; but even the best of people have their demons talking in their ears and James is honestly fighting his demons – desperately;<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“Instead he was handsome the way you think of the devil as handsome – forbiddingly so.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br>- <b>Filippa</b> is the only one of the three girls of the group whom I actually love; she’s always seen as the <i>extra</i> – she is too volatile to fit into a category so that gives her the ability to play many roles, on- and offstage; <i>Beware of the ones who seldom speak because they are the ones who held many secrets and truths;</i><br>- <b>Alexander</b> is a freakshow really, a junkhead and definitely the <i>villain</i> of the story, but he might be the one you’ll go to when you want to forget about your worries; he exudes this calmness that you cannot grasp, but you definitely need in life;<br>- <b>Wren</b> is such a weird character, it was a bit hard for me to love her; I liked her enough but there was something unpleasant about her that I just couldn’t place and so I have no developed opinion about her; she seems, somehow, too unstable, fragile; the ingénue of the group maybe;<br>- <b>Meredith</b> is definitely the temptress, the femme fatale; she’s the she-devil of the story, tempting everyone with her perfect figure like she’s some sort of sexual goddess walking on Earth amongst mortals; I, for once, didn’t like her almost at all; even though I sometimes felt sorry for her, I only saw her as being fake first of all to herself and then to the other around her; I wanted to like her, but I couldn’t, she was lying to herself and she only played with the others to make herself feel better;<br>- <b>Richard</b> is the tyrant and the only character that I truly despised from the beginning; no matter how talented you are, what a promising rising star you might be, if you’re not a decent human being, then you’re nothing; and Richard is absolutely disgusting as a day-to-day person and I couldn’t like him in any way.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“Actors are by nature volatile—alchemic creatures composed of incendiary elements, emotion and ego and envy. Heat them up, stir them together, and sometimes you get gold. Sometimes disaster.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1588080477i/29370304._SY540_.gif" width="252" height="366" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>From the moment six of them discover the body of the seventh, an unforgiving road leading to self-depreciation opens up before all of them. They slowly start to degrade, both morally and physically. They become unsettled and cold. They have to make decisions that might alter their lives forever. They start making decisions no one has to make in life.<br><br>This book is terribly deep if you really pay attention to everything that’s happening. It warns you about abuse, about obsession, about death and about the decisions we can make avoid certain situations; it is about what love looks like – it might be a friend, it might be a sister, it might be loyalty, in the end.<br><br>This book talks about love, either desperate, hopeless, mad or even platonic love. Impossible love. It talks about sacrifice and whatever it is that leads one to do it. It talks about the fine line that stands between <b>real</b> and <b>not real</b> in the life of troubled, artistic and wild souls.<br><br>This book is beautiful. Like, truly beautiful. And if you got a chance to read it, then read it with your mind and heart open, not only with your eyes. Because there is so much more to it than simply words.<br><br>In the end, it doesn’t matter you enjoy the drama, because everything turns into a careful tragic masterpiece with no chance of changing its ending.<br><br>I honestly fell in love with this. You might too.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“But that is how a tragedy like ours or King Lear breaks your heart – by making you believe that the ending might still be happy, until the very last minute.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>(<a href="https://urcdn.eu/styles/8413155d-37dc-453b-80a1-b3a1a25fe4c5_original?b" rel="nofollow noopener">Book-styled</a>)</span>
  <a data-text-id="15913266500595153851" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2532335601" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2532335601" />
    <a title="Melanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie"><img alt="Melanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577914102p2/3030788.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2532335601?book_show_action=true">Sep 30, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie">Melanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=lgbtqiap">lgbtqiap</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=buddy-reads">buddy-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2532335601" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1611249891944954976"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1539891145i/26468232._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“You can justify anything if you do it poetically enough.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>This book is so haunting, so atmospheric, so gripping, and so perfect. And If you, too, love <a href='https://meltotheany.wordpress.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Secret History by Donna Tartt</a> then I recommend this book with every single bone in my body. Also, this is such a love letter to Shakespeare and all his work, so if you appreciate that I think you’ll also fall so head over heels for this story. I’m honestly not sure what I expected going into <i>If We Were Villains</i>, but it is now one </span>
  <span id="freeText1611249891944954976" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1539891145i/26468232._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“You can justify anything if you do it poetically enough.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>This book is so haunting, so atmospheric, so gripping, and so perfect. And If you, too, love <a href="https://meltotheany.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">The Secret History by Donna Tartt</a> then I recommend this book with every single bone in my body. Also, this is such a love letter to Shakespeare and all his work, so if you appreciate that I think you’ll also fall so head over heels for this story. I’m honestly not sure what I expected going into <i>If We Were Villains</i>, but it is now one of my favorite books of all time. <br><br>This story follows seven very pretentious theater students, going to a very prestigious and private college. They moved to Ohio to go to the university from all over the world, but they really made a found family with each other, while all living in what they call the Castle on campus. But one night their life completely changes when they all come together on a decision that alters their fate. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Nothing mattered much after that morning. Our two souls—if not all six—were forfeit.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>➽ <b>Richard</b> - has a bad temper and is the “mean” one. <br><br>➽ <b>Meredith</b> - Richard’s girlfriend, and the “sexy vixen” type. <br> <br>➽ <b>Filippa</b> - The “cool” one, in my opinion. Mysterious home life. My second favorite.<br><br>➽ <b>Alexander</b> - Gay, grew up in foster care, and I believe is Latinx. Yet, is the “stoner” one. <br><br>➽ <b>Wren</b> - Richard’s cousin, and “the girl next-door” type. <br><br>➽ <b>James</b> - The best actor and our main protagonist’s roommate. I’d say the “popular” one.<br> <br>➽ <b>Oliver</b> - Our main protagonist, who is nice, and who is sweet, and who just wants to keep the peace between his group of friends. Also, Oliver is totally pansexual and no one can change my mind on this. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“My infatuation […] transcended any notion of gender.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Oliver is for sure the main character, and this book starts out with him getting out of prison ten years after the events of that frightful night. And he is finally telling the story of what actually happened. This book is also broken up in five acts, but we get to see the events of what really happened that night, a decade ago, and we get to see the ramifications of how that altered everyone’s lives in present day. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“How tremendous the agony of unmade decisions.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>And each act, to me, really highlights a different Shakespearean play, that really sets the tone for what is unfolding in that act. From <i> A Midsummer Night's Dream</i>, to <i>Julius Caesar</i>, to <i>King Lear</i>, to <i>Romeo and Juliet</i>, to so many more; the honoring, appreciation, and celebration are all there and it truly makes for a read like no other. This book is a love letter to theater. And this book is structured so perfectly, written so expertly, that I really think that R.L. Rio crafted something beyond genius. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“It’s easier now to be Romeo, or Macbeth, or Brutus, or Edmund. Someone else.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Friends, I feel like this is a book that won’t be for everyone, but if it is for you then you will love it with the sum of your being. This was perfection for me, and completely made my October this year. If you’re looking for something haunting, and thrilling, and so very atmospheric, then please give <i>If We Were Villains</i> a try. And that last line? It is going to haunt me forever with its beautiful perfection. <br><br><a href="https://meltotheany.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/meltotheany/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.twitter.com/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://meltotheany.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UC4RbHEg_fH6CewJrh_0xJ9g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="http://www.twitch.tv/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitch</a> <br><br><b>Content and trigger warnings</b> for: death, murder, physical abuse, slut shaming, a transphobic comment, a onetime use of the slur for Romani people, a homophobic comment, drug overdose, PTSD depiction, depression depiction, suicide, self-harm, and mention of an eating disorder (and a poor taste comment about it).<br><br>Buddy read for <a href="https://meltotheany.com/2018/09/24/fridayfrightathon-2018/" rel="nofollow noopener">#FridayFrightAThon</a> which I co-hosted with <a href="https://acourtofcrownsandquills.wordpress.com/2018/09/23/blanca-y-roja-by-anna-marie-mclemore/" rel="nofollow noopener">Amy @ A Court of Crowns and Quills</a>, <a href="https://pinotandpages247.wordpress.com/2018/09/23/arc-review-shadow-of-the-fox/" rel="nofollow noopener">Jen @ Pinot and Pages</a>, &amp; <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=otwtCWoDoNs" rel="nofollow noopener">Chelsea @ Chelsea Palmer</a>! 👻</span>
  <a data-text-id="1611249891944954976" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1969332082" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1969332082" />
    <a title="Charlotte May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14002983-charlotte-may"><img alt="Charlotte May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596906925p2/14002983.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1969332082?book_show_action=true">Mar 27, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Charlotte May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Charlotte May" href="/user/show/14002983-charlotte-may">Charlotte May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781785656477" href="/book/show/34369803-if-we-were-villains">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=tear-jerker">tear-jerker</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=alcoholism-drugs">alcoholism-drugs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=crime-mystery-thriller">crime-mystery-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=illness-mental-terminal">illness-mental-terminal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1969332082" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4451844600306844224"><i> "This thing of darkness I acknowledge mine." </i><br/><br/>I have no words. I expected this to be good - there are so many exceptional reviews, I really hoped it would live up to its hype.<br/>Well, it did and more!<br/>7 drama students at an Elite Arts University are in their final year. They are as close as 7 people can be, they fight, they love and above it all they are obsessed with the works of Shakespeare (bear this in mind if you don't like Shakespeare as there are loads of quotes and sections in here).<br/><br/>Oliver -</span>
  <span id="freeText4451844600306844224" style="display:none"><i> "This thing of darkness I acknowledge mine." </i><br /><br />I have no words. I expected this to be good - there are so many exceptional reviews, I really hoped it would live up to its hype.<br />Well, it did and more!<br />7 drama students at an Elite Arts University are in their final year. They are as close as 7 people can be, they fight, they love and above it all they are obsessed with the works of Shakespeare (bear this in mind if you don't like Shakespeare as there are loads of quotes and sections in here).<br /><br />Oliver - Our main protagonist, describes himself as the least talented of the group. The most ordinary.<br /><br />James - Oliver's room mate and best friend, they have been inseparable for the last four years.<br /><br />Meredith - The vixen. Described constantly as this impossibly attractive woman, no man is immune. Every part she has ever played has invoked this sexual aura she seems to have.<br /><br />Richard - Dating Meredith. The absolute epitamy of the shortened version of his name (aka Dick). I hated this guy with a passion, he is arrogant, rude and violent. He usually gets the main part in every show they put on.<br /><br />Wren - Richard's cousin, a delicate flower. Another reviewer described her as 'the girl next door' which I think is a good description for her.<br /><br />Filippa - A bit mysterious. She never reveals her home life, keeps mainly to herself but she is fiercely loyal to the others.<br /><br />The book opens with Oliver about to leave prison after a decade, serving time for murder. Detective Colborne - the police officer who arrested Oliver, has never really believed his story. Now he is about to retire, he asks Oliver if he will finally tell the truth about what really happened all those years ago.<br /><br />We are swept up into the students' world of parties, drugs, obsessions and secrets. And honestly? It is so addictive - there is this underlying theme of darkness, we know something bad is going to happen, it's just a matter of when.<br /><br />The ending wasn't quite the twist I was hoping for. But then again, it had to be someone so there couldn't really have been any other ending without it becoming unrealistic, so I think it was done well. I was also heartbroken when <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Filippa tells Oliver that James' committed suicide a few years before - he couldn't handle the guilt anymore. Though the final page does leave the possibility that maybe he didn't die? Potentially. I like that idea  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Overall, I thought this was fantastic, and I highly recommend it. Murder mystery mixed in with the drama of the theatre and the passion of Shakespeare. What's not to love?<br /><br /><i> "When we first walked through those doors, we did so without knowing that we were now part of some strange fanatic religion where anything could be excused so long as it was offered at the altar of the Muses. Ritual madness, ecstasy, human sacrifice. Were we bewitched? Brainwashed? Perhaps." </i><br /><br /><br />************************************************<br /><br />So this book just ruined me. I’m going to need much time to recover from this.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2377302969" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2377302969" />
    <a title="✨    jamieson   ✨" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7706640-jamieson"><img alt="✨    jamieson   ✨" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499961431p2/7706640.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2377302969?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="✨    jamieson   ✨" class="user" itemprop="url" name="✨    jamieson   ✨" href="/user/show/7706640-jamieson">✨    jamieson   ✨</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781785656477" href="/book/show/34369803-if-we-were-villains">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=owned-books">owned-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=2019-reads">2019-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=lgbtqiap">lgbtqiap</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=bi-mc">bi-mc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=m-m">m-m</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2377302969" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15598715296805595414"><br/><b>To sum up:</b> This is the secret history, but written better and with less queerbait, and it focusses on Shakespeare not Greek myths. Dark Academia is That Genre, I love it so much and it fuels me. I'm so glad I finally read this, it was truly delicious. Also, I'm talking about my Theory for the end in the last past of this review to stay tuned, folks!<br/><br/><i>
  <blockquote>“The real sky was enormous overhead, making our mirrors and twinkling stage lights seem ridiculous- Man’s futile attempt to imitate God” </blockquote>
</i><br/><br/><br/><u>If We We</u></span>
  <span id="freeText15598715296805595414" style="display:none"><br /><b>To sum up:</b> This is the secret history, but written better and with less queerbait, and it focusses on Shakespeare not Greek myths. Dark Academia is That Genre, I love it so much and it fuels me. I'm so glad I finally read this, it was truly delicious. Also, I'm talking about my Theory for the end in the last past of this review to stay tuned, folks!<br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>“The real sky was enormous overhead, making our mirrors and twinkling stage lights seem ridiculous- Man’s futile attempt to imitate God” </blockquote>
</i><br /><br /><br /><u>If We Were Villains</u> follows Oliver, who has just been released from prison. The lead investigator on his case ten years ago, who has now quit the police, begs Oliver to reveal the truth of what happened on the fateful party that landed Oliver in prison ten years ago. And so begins a tale of friends who attend an elite acting school for Shakespeare, where the characters and words they become every day start to distort their own perceptions of themselves. <br /><br />This is Such excellent dark academia, exploring the power of words and characters and emotion. I love Shakespeare, so I love how this focussed on his works and integrated the plays and the meanings of his works into the book. The focus on emotion and pathos, central to Shakespeare, becomes central here. I loved the way the author translated the contemporary idolisation of Shakespeare into something so dark and twisted. I also loved that the author incorporated Shakespeare's style into the book. For example, writing dialogue like a play script, and including themes, motifs and dialogue from plays into the text. If We Were Villains makes sense if you haven't read Shakespeare, but I think it's enriched in a huge way if you HAVE read his works. I think it was a cool choice - the inside Shakespeare jokes and callbacks makes you feel just as pretentious and clever as the characters, and it's just a really fun dynamic to play with. <br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>“Which of us could say we were more sinned against than sinning? We were so easily manipulated - confusion made a masterpiece of us.” </blockquote>
</i><br /><br />All in all, we follow main characters. At first, I do think they're a bit stereotypical and cliche, but I thought Rio did a good job at exploring these cliches, and analysing why and how people categorise characters and people. <br /><br />➽ Oliver - The main character. He's the 'good guy', generally nice, just wants everyone to be friends and keep the peace. He is a bit naive, a little bit unsure of himself, but as likeable as these characters can be. <br /><br />➽ James - Oliver's roommate and best friend. He's popular, a great actor, and usually gets the great, tragic hero roles. <br /><br />➽ Richard - Truly, lives up to his dick nickname. The Henry Winters, if you will. But the teachers favourite, and gets all the heroic hero roles. <br /><br />➽ Alexander - The funny friend. He's gay and latinx. Known for partying/drinking/drugs. He was one of my favouries because he was so funny. Usually gets the funny side character parts. <br /><br />➽ Meredith - Richard’s girlfriend. "The sexy, sultry woman". She gets all the best female roles. <br /><br />➽ Filippa - Mysterious and nice. No one knows much about her, but she gets along well with Oliver. She, like Oliver, usually gets the leftover parts because no one really knows what 'her thing' is. <br /><br />➽ Wren - Richard’s cousin, relaxed and moderate, usually trying to be the balance between Richard and the rest of the group. She is pretty close with James. <br /><br />One thing I really liked was how the characters typecasts in terms of Shakespeare plays both informed and distorted their characterisation. The characters almost 'become' their parts, making it hard to determine where their acting and their actual personality begins and ends. Perhaps acting is personality and personality is acted and it's all the same? Those are the kind of questions Rio poses throughout this book, leading to her characters becoming increasingly complex and hard to pin-down throughout the book. I thought the way she undermined but also played into the stereotypes - from tragic hero, to the seductress, to funny sidekick, to loyal best friend - was really interesting, and a way of drawing out characterisation I really haven't seen before. Also, the way the characters are trying to escape their assigned destinies if they aren't good - eg, tragic hero - really made my heart hurt. When [ THAT CHARACTER ] said he doesn't want to be a tragic hero again, he wants to be the hero of a romantic comedy. Wow, MY HEART. <br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>"Do you blame Shakespeare for any of it?"<br />"I blame him for all of it."<br /></blockquote>
</i><br /><br />The writing in <b>If We Were Villains</b> was also really beautiful. I found myself tabbing A LOT of this book because it was so wonderfully written. The prose was a good balance of pretentious and flowery, a hallmark of the genre, but not overly incomprehensible. I also loved how the atmosphere and setting were established. Rio created such a tacit and tangible setting, with the smells and the pictures and the tone so easy to picture. I liked how she took Shakespearean conventions to establish elements of the story, blending prose and play in such a clever way. The <br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>“The sky was clear and quiet, stars peering curiously down at us from a wide dome of indigo. The water, too, was still, and I thought, what liars they are, the sky and the water. Still and calm and clear, like everything was fine. It wasn’t fine, and really, it never would be again.”<br /></blockquote>
</i><br /><br />Anyways, I just really loved this book so much. A true treat and delight for those of us who love Shakespeare and art and love to Feel Emotions but like, can't handle it. Also, I was living for the m/m romance-ish kinda thing happening, and I would literally die for Oliver and his happiness. Anyways, if you like atmospheric books, angst, the secret history, shakespeare, shaky friendships, and drama, you should read this book. <br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><b>OKAY AND NOW I'M TALKING ABOUT MY THEORY ON THE END SO SPOILERS</b> !!! 🚨🚨<br />🚨🚨🚨🚨<br /><br />Alright. James is Alive and Well. And here is my defence of that statement<br /><br />Listen, I'm going to give y'all a quick sum up of Pericles. <br />Basically, Pericles has both a wife and a daughter he thinks are dead for the majority of the play. He sails into the ocean to die because he thinks everyone he loves is gone, but he then finds out that his wife and daughter, are actually alive, and the final part of the play is Pericles being reunited with them both. Pericles is an interesting play because it is set up like a tragedy but ends up like a comedy - aka, in the Shakespearean comedies, the drama is resolved when the characters who are presumed to be dead turn out to be alive, or when two characters kept apart by circumstances end up getting married. <br /><br />SO, how does it all relate? One, James says Oliver is Pericles, which is significant because Pericles is the only tragic hero who actually gets a happy ending. Instead of everyone dying, he gets everyone back in the end. Second, James sending the Pericles letter is important because it refers to the bit where Pericles thinks he will be drowned at sea with his wife, only to discover she never drowned at sea and is alive. Like, Pericles is The Hero who actually gets everything back, even when everyone thinks both he and his whole family are dead. Also, James says at one point he's done playing the tragic hero and wants to do a comedy instead, which is when everyone gets to be happy at the end. FINALLY, James and Richard are both likened to the Sparrow in Hamlet, and the sparrow is a metaphor for fleeing to somewhere where you can be guilt-free and escape your past. <br /><br />ANYWAYS, maybe I'm reaching but I Just Want Them To Be Happy so yes I do intend to read every fanfic of this in the world and live in bliss imagining this until I day. Have a good day, sir!</span>
  <a data-text-id="15598715296805595414" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1976227804" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7006327075885665966">As someone who’s not familiar with theatre plays, I still enjoyed reading this book regardless. I’m sure theatre lovers will pick up all the nuances and appreciate it more, but it’s a fun ride with all the murder and melodrama, and I could still tell that much of the narrative mirrored plays that the characters were performing and quoting. There was a lot of building tension and intrigue throughout the story, though I felt the plot twist and the murder’s identity were predictable.</span>

<div id="review_1945576194" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1945576194" />
    <a title="karen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45618-karen"><img alt="karen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596291582p2/45618.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1945576194?book_show_action=true">Mar 18, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="karen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="karen" href="/user/show/45618-karen">karen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=books-claiming-to-be-like-secret-hi">books-claiming-to-be-like-secret-hi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1945576194" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13250169505424988427">until the ending, this was probably going to be a three star from me. a high three on the three-star spectrum, but a three nonetheless. it held my interest, but i think this one will resonate more with theater-kids than it did for me, because of how firmly entrenched it is in that world. rio makes it accessible to regular folk, but it probably helps to have a soft place in your heart for young actors and the things that drive them, and i’m someone impatient with affectation both in life and in m</span>
  <span id="freeText13250169505424988427" style="display:none">until the ending, this was probably going to be a three star from me. a high three on the three-star spectrum, but a three nonetheless. it held my interest, but i think this one will resonate more with theater-kids than it did for me, because of how firmly entrenched it is in that world. rio makes it accessible to regular folk, but it probably helps to have a soft place in your heart for young actors and the things that drive them, and i’m someone impatient with affectation both in life and in my reading, so the characters were frequently more grating than charming to me. they’re definitely convincing for who they are, but i never warmed to any of them or felt sympathetic towards them - i’ve certainly known people like this in my life, but it’s exhausting to be confronted with <i>seven</i> of them at once, all posturing and pretentious banter, where conversations are on-the-nose passages from shakespeare’s plays shot back-and-forth, displaying the characters' education, not necessarily their personality. <br><br>i’m with the detective (the first speaker) in this scene:<br><br><blockquote>”So,” he says. “How much of what you told me about that night was true?”<br><br>“All of it,” I say, “in one way or another.”<br><br>A pause. “Are we going to play this game?”<br><br><i>”Wherein I am false I am honest; not true, to be true,”</i> I say.<br><br>“I thought they would have beaten that bullshit out of you in prison.”<br><br>“That bullshit is all that kept me going.” One thing I’m sure Colborne will never understand is that I need language to live, like food - lexemes and morphemes and morsels of meaning nourish me with the knowledge that, yes, there is a word for this. Someone else has felt this before.<br><br>“Why don’t you just tell me what happened? No performance. No poetics.”<br><br>“For us, everything was a performance.” A small, private smile catches me off guard and I glance down, hoping he won’t see it. “Everything poetic.”<br><br>Colborne is quiet for a moment and then says, “You win. Tell it your way.”</blockquote><br><br>to backtrack, this book is a variant on <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29044.The_Secret_History" title="The Secret History by Donna Tartt" rel="nofollow noopener">The Secret History</a> theme - it features seven theater students in their fourth year at a very elite arts college whose discipline is strictly shakespeare. they live together in an appropriately dramatic castle-like structure, slightly off the main campus - inseparable from each other, isolated from 'normal' people, and constantly immersed in tragedies filled with feuds, vengeance, and casual murders. further complications result from the particulars of the actor’s temperament:<br><br><blockquote>”A good Shakespearian actor - a good actor of any stripe, really - doesn’t just <i>say</i> words, he <i>feels</i> them. We all felt the passions of the characters we played as if they were our own. But a character’s emotions don’t cancel out the actor’s - instead you feel both at once. Imagine having all your own thoughts and feelings tangled up with all the thoughts and feelings of a whole other person. It can be hard, sometimes, to sort out which is which.”</blockquote><br><br>considering this perfect storm of elements, it’s not surprising when life and art get blurred and one of them ends up dead. but is it the result of an accident or murrrrrderrrr? the events of that night are murky, but our verbiage-spouting narrator oliver marks confessed to the murder and has spent the past ten years in jail. his release coincides with the retirement of detective colborne, the lead investigator in the case, and oliver is ready to tell colborne exactly what happened that night. his way.<br><br>the story is split between oliver ‘now,’ returning to the scene of the crime with colborne, and the story of everything that went on in this cult-like group ten years ago; of a group of people obsessed with shakespeare whose relationships with each other were as complicated as any tragedy - resentments and rivalries, sexual dalliances, unrequited longing, blood relatives and lovers, straight and gay, addictions and insecurities and the fine line between acting and lying, onstage combat and real-life consequences.<br><br>it’s a debut, so there’s some first-timer clumsiness in terms of exposition - the first chapter, introducing all the players is kind of tedious, but it definitely picks up once it gets over the basic stage-setting. the scenery-chewing shakespeare stuff is a bit indulgent; shakespeare ends up doing a lot of the narrative work in what is often a pretty straightforward story, if you’ve read a lot of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29044.The_Secret_History" title="The Secret History by Donna Tartt" rel="nofollow noopener">The Secret History</a> <i>type</i> books, but there’s one interesting spin on the story: usually the narrator in these books takes the ‘outsider looking in’ role, typically separated from the group at large because of a lower socio-economic status, but in this case - yes, oliver is much less well-off than most of his peers, but i think each of the characters could claim outsider status for one reason or another, and the group is less cohesive than <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29044.The_Secret_History" title="The Secret History by Donna Tartt" rel="nofollow noopener">The Secret History</a> norm (although it does mirror the character checklist of two <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[possibly incestuous <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> relatives; cousins, not twins, one gay male, and one major asshole)<br><br>it's a good read; if you're a <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29044.The_Secret_History" title="The Secret History by Donna Tartt" rel="nofollow noopener">The Secret History</a> readalike addict like me, it's not going to blow your mind, but it's entertaining, and i did really like the little turn at the end. it opens up a lot of questions about what will happen next, but it was a nice little surprise in a story i thought had already ended. <br><br>three and a half rounded up, and i will gladly read anything else she writes.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1528725630i/25720315.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><a href="http://bloggycomelately.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">come to my blog!</a></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="13250169505424988427" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
