<div id="review_1942825522" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1942825522" />
    <a title="Amalia Gkavea" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/56789747-amalia-gkavea"><img alt="Amalia Gkavea" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559158764p2/56789747.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1942825522?book_show_action=true">Jun 04, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amalia Gkavea" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amalia Gkavea" href="/user/show/56789747-amalia-gkavea">Amalia Gkavea</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/32874746-if-we-were-villains">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56789747-amalia-gkavea?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56789747-amalia-gkavea?shelf=american-literature">american-literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56789747-amalia-gkavea?shelf=shakespeare">shakespeare</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56789747-amalia-gkavea?shelf=theatre">theatre</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56789747-amalia-gkavea?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56789747-amalia-gkavea?shelf=usa">usa</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56789747-amalia-gkavea?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56789747-amalia-gkavea?shelf=crime">crime</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1942825522" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7678199063803824440"><i>
  <b>‘’’Tis now dead midnight.’’<br/>			Measure for Measure, Act 4, Scene 2</b>
</i><br/> <br/>Why midnight?Midnight stands between light and darkness. The day that has been completed and the new one that slowly attempts to rise. During midnight, two key events take place in this glorious book, and like this haunting time of day, our characters are walking the thin line between good and evil. And for this, they make the best ‘’villains’’.<br/> <br/>This book is so exquisite,so darkly beautiful that I didn’t want it to end. What f</span>
  <span id="freeText7678199063803824440" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>‘’’Tis now dead midnight.’’<br />			Measure for Measure, Act 4, Scene 2</b>
</i><br /> <br />Why midnight?Midnight stands between light and darkness. The day that has been completed and the new one that slowly attempts to rise. During midnight, two key events take place in this glorious book, and like this haunting time of day, our characters are walking the thin line between good and evil. And for this, they make the best ‘’villains’’.<br /> <br />This book is so exquisite,so darkly beautiful that I didn’t want it to end. What fascinated me more was the fact that it is not only an ode to the immortal genius that is Shakespeare, but a hymn to the significance and immense value of the Villain. Well-written villains are the crown jewels in Literature and a large majority of readers find them absolutely fascinating as they have shaped -and continue shaping- Literature and Theatre. Shakespeare’s villains, in particular, are the core of his greatest plays. Is Macbeth a villain? Or Shylock? What about Brutus or Edmund? Or Iago who seems to have absolutely no redeeming qualities?<br /> <br />In M.L.Rio’s novel, we have seven four-year students that are about to graduate and become actors in the real world. A tragic event following a short period of intense feelings causes their world to tumble down. Passions and hidden animosity come forward and the villains become victims and the victims are turned to villains on their own freewill.<br /> <br /><i>
  <b>‘’By the pricking of my thumbs, something wicked this way comes.’’<br />			Macbeth, Act 4 , Scene 1</b>
</i><br /><br />M.L. Rio manages to use and refer to every play by the Bard and some of his sonnets, but there are four plays which shape the narrative.<i>Macbeth</i>, <i>Julius Caesar</i>, <i>King Lear</i>, <i>Romeo and Juliet</i>. Each one serves a different purpose and Rio works them in the story masterfully. Wicked deeds are set in motion when a member of this fellowship loses the sense of right and wrong, and as in <i>Julius Caesar</i>, the battle between friends and the acts that can be considered treasonous consist the essence of the entire story. The theme of problematic friendship is present in <i>Macbeth</i> as well, where Macbeth turns against his loyal friend, Banquo, guided by ambition and a misleading wish for power. Perhaps, <i>Macbeth</i> is the play most presented and quoted in the novel, something that contributes to its foreboding beauty. There is a sequence of a production of the Scottish Play, set during the night of Halloween, in the darkness, outdoors. It is among the most beautiful and most powerful depictions I've ever read or watched. Theatre directors should definitely consult Rio before they attempt to deal with <i>Macbeth</i>. I’d dare to say that the Bard himself would certainly embrace it. It is an eerie, haunting scene, an exaltation of Will’s masterpiece.<br /> <br /><i>
  <b>‘’Believe none of us.’’<br />			Hamlet, Act 3, Scene 1</b>
</i><br /> <br />Yes, the seven friends are among the most interesting characters you’ll come across. They are not to be trusted, or believed, but you must care for them. Richard is wild, possessive, the male star of the company.Wren is delicate and shy, the Ophelia of the group. Alexander doesn't really know what to do with his life, James knows what to do but is too afraid to do it. The three most interesting characters are Oliver, Meredith and Filipa.Meredith is my spirit animal. Fierce, demanding, questioning everything, but sensitive and always uncertain of herself and her abilities. I love her! Filipa is a beautiful soul, loyal, tender, the rock that keeps everyone solid, struggling for them to retain their sanity. Oliver is the heat of the story, he is kindness and innocence and the proof that there is still some good in this world that cannot be destroyed. Poor Oliver…<br /> <br />The writing is exceptional! Oliver’s speech on the essence of Shakespeare is the best I’ve ever read. The whole spirit of the Bard enclosed in a short paragraph, better than any collection of academic essays. Modern language interacts with Shakespeare’s immortal lines in a brilliant flow of speech.<br /> <br />There are so many incredible twists, so much insight into the human soul. What about lies? Lies that are used to protect loved ones? Lies that we have taken for granted for all our lives? Who is the villain?Shakespeare knew human nature better than any psychologist. He knew that there is no clear line between a villain and victim. Just as it often happens in real life. And this is so beautifully transferred in Rio’s marvelous novel that makes one wonder whether we actually know where our ‘’good’’ self end and the ‘’bad’’ begins. This duality is a never-ending battle…<br /> <br />This is a beautiful, moving book, created with darkness, strife and sensitivity. Read it and see for yourselves…<br /> <br /><i>
  <b>''When shall we three meet again? In thunder, lightning, or in rain?''<br />''When the hurlyburly’s done. When the battle’s lost and won.''<br />			Macbeth, Act 1, Scene 1</b>
</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="7678199063803824440" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2136686381" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2136686381" />
    <a title="Julie " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5210022-julie"><img alt="Julie " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1356906542p2/5210022.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2136686381?book_show_action=true">Sep 27, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie " href="/user/show/5210022-julie">Julie </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/32874746-if-we-were-villains">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=overdrive">overdrive</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=e-book">e-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=flatiron-books">flatiron-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=thrillers">thrillers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=mystery-shelf">mystery-shelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=added-by-recommendation">added-by-recommendation</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=crime">crime</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2136686381" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10985710523490731918">If We Were Villains by M.L. Rio is a 2017 Flatiron Books publication. <br/><br/><br/>This is a psychological thriller for deep thinkers. There is crime and there is punishment. There is mystery, suspense. There are intense characters, shallow ones too, those who are fatalistic and those who are tragic… just like a Shakespearean play.<br/><br/><br/>Ten years ago, Oliver Marks was one of seven Shakespearean actors at the prestigious Dellecher Classical Conservatory. Today he is about to walk out of a prison cell for the first </span>
  <span id="freeText10985710523490731918" style="display:none">If We Were Villains by M.L. Rio is a 2017 Flatiron Books publication. <br /><br /><br />This is a psychological thriller for deep thinkers. There is crime and there is punishment. There is mystery, suspense. There are intense characters, shallow ones too, those who are fatalistic and those who are tragic… just like a Shakespearean play.<br /><br /><br />Ten years ago, Oliver Marks was one of seven Shakespearean actors at the prestigious Dellecher Classical Conservatory. Today he is about to walk out of a prison cell for the first time in a decade. How did he end up behind bars? <br /><br />That’s something Detective Colbourne would also like to know. He may have put Oliver in prison, but he knows there is more to the story than he's been told. <br /><br />He can’t rest until he coaxes the entire story out of Oliver once and for all. With Colbourne retired, and with nothing else to lose, Oliver grants Colbourne his wish. <br /><br /><b>‘But that I am forbid/ To tell the secrets of my prison -house,/ I could a tale unfold whose lightest word/ Would horrow up thy soul.’</b><br /><br />The story then flashes back ten years as Oliver walks us through the events that left him holding the bag for crimes he may or may not have been solely responsible for. <br /><br />When one of the seven elite actors’ dies, the remaining six thespians are the very picture of innocence. It was an accident after all… wasn’t it? But, Detective Colbourne’s senses they know more than they are telling. Are they as innocent as they appear or are they harboring a dark secret- one that is eating away at them more and more with each passing day?<br /><br />I tend to gravitate towards these types of stories, which are too few and far between, but I suppose that only makes me appreciate them even more when I stumble across one. <br /><br />The Shakespearean allegory is well done, as the stage is set for the ultimate tragedy. Our little acting coalition is as thick as thieves, too close, too driven, too immersed within their own little thespian world to cope with reality as most of us know it, which leads to grave consequences, when they begin to become the roles they often play on stage. Jealousy, competition, unrequited love, anger and resentment stir the bubbling pot until ‘exuent omnes’. <br /><br />I was so engrossed in Oliver’s tale, so mortified, so mesmerized and tantalized, and despite knowing most of the details of the crime in question, and that Oliver has obviously paid his debt, the suspense is still nearly unbearable, because I still didn't know WHY- or HOW things turned out this way. I was filled with such dread, I almost felt like I was back in Vermont at Hamden College listening to Richard Papen unfold a similarly horrifying tale of obsession. <br /><br />But, as morally questionable as those standing center stage may be, as superficial and self-absorbed, or in some cases, as honorable, or heroic- the classic “Villains VS Heroes”, if you will, the story is haunting and left a painful ache in my heart. <br /><br /><b>“But that is how a tragedy like ours or King Lear breaks your heart- by making you believe that the ending might still be happy, until the very last minute.”</b><br /><br /><br />The author did an amazing job with presentation and ‘staging’, as such, and created a vivid atmosphere, perfect for settling in for a modern Shakespearean tragedy. If you are a fan of the Bard, you will really appreciate the way the dialogue mirrors the events as they unfold and of course the bittersweet irony. <br /><br />This is not just a psychological thriller, it’s a literary novel filled with obsessions and angst, with beauty and horror, and a near pitch perfect delivery! <br /><br />This is a debut novel, incredibly, and I for one am pretty much blown away! <br /><br />Pulling out the stars for this one! <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10985710523490731918" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1979088606" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1979088606" />
    <a title="K. Elizabeth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17568354-k-elizabeth"><img alt="K. Elizabeth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1606078931p2/17568354.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1979088606?book_show_action=true">Sep 06, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="K. Elizabeth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="K. Elizabeth" href="/user/show/17568354-k-elizabeth">K. Elizabeth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Those who enjoyed &quot;The Secret History,&quot; by Donna Tart</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17568354-k-elizabeth?shelf=imaginative">imaginative</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17568354-k-elizabeth?shelf=5-stars">5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17568354-k-elizabeth?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17568354-k-elizabeth?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17568354-k-elizabeth?shelf=memorable-characters">memorable-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17568354-k-elizabeth?shelf=painful-withdrawals">painful-withdrawals</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17568354-k-elizabeth?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17568354-k-elizabeth?shelf=original-idea">original-idea</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17568354-k-elizabeth?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17568354-k-elizabeth?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1979088606" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7402367360841308901">*Update - 2018*<br/><br/>Because I still think about this book almost a year after reading it, I'm moving it to my favorite's shelf. I think it's deserving there, right alongside <i>The Secret History</i> and <i>Vicious</i>.<br/>___________________________________<br/><br/><b>4.25-4.5/5 Stars</b><br/><br/><b>
  <u>This was breathtakingly brilliant.</u>
</b> Honestly, if this book isn't on your to-be-read list, <i>it needs to be.</i> It starts off shaky (at least it did to me), however, once it grabs your attention - it will not let go.<br/><br/>Now, where do I even start? Should I</span>
  <span id="freeText7402367360841308901" style="display:none">*Update - 2018*<br /><br />Because I still think about this book almost a year after reading it, I'm moving it to my favorite's shelf. I think it's deserving there, right alongside <i>The Secret History</i> and <i>Vicious</i>.<br />___________________________________<br /><br /><b>4.25-4.5/5 Stars</b><br /><br /><b>
  <u>This was breathtakingly brilliant.</u>
</b> Honestly, if this book isn't on your to-be-read list, <i>it needs to be.</i> It starts off shaky (at least it did to me), however, once it grabs your attention - it will not let go.<br /><br />Now, where do I even start? Should I start with how layered these characters are? (Though, I will say, I noticed the female characters could've used more depth). Should I begin with how flawlessly Rio tied in multiple Shakespearean plays into the actual plot? Or maybe, I should talk about the mystery/tension intertwined with everything that occurs throughout this novel? <br /><br />You know what? <br /><br />I'm going to ramble.<br /><br />So. This story revolves around 7 students who are majoring in Shakespearean Studies &amp; Acting (something like that) - and from the beginning you realize that this degree and school is no joke. It's competitive. Serious. Cut throat. Which makes it all the more intriguing. It wouldn't be half as good of a story if it took place at a "nicer school."<br /><br />Getting right to it, I <i>loved</i> how every character had something going for them. Though, at first, it was difficult remembering who was who, and it sometimes bothered me that I couldn't picture anyone. <i>However,</i> those things hardly deterred me from continuing (surprisingly). The plot and depth of the characters made up for everything else. So don't be fooled and think that these characters are just your "shallow" sort of college students. In some ways, they might be. However, they're much more.<br /><br />Something else that I LOVED, was the strange/strong relationship between James and Oliver. When I was reading, I kept on wondering why the <i>heck</i> I wanted them to end up together. Quite badly, too. I mean, by all appearances they were just friends. Plus, Oliver was head-over-heals for Meredith. And yet, I couldn't help but feel that while he lusted after Meredith, he had a very real passion for James. Just like Oliver himself says (towards the end), he himself had no idea what he and James were. Whatever it was, it was bloody brilliant.<br /><br />Unfortunately, this book didn't end up in my "all time favorites." I thought it would have. Really. However, when I looked at everything, there were some dull spats throughout the story. Plus, I couldn't ignore how most of the male characters had layered personalities, whereas the female characters seemed bland. (Except perhaps Meredith, she played a big role - but in a stereotypical way).<br /><br />Overall, I feel like I've given away too much - and not enough. I wish I could ramble more, but I feel like I'm not doing the story justice. I'll probably comes back and re-review this. <br /><br />In the meantime, get this book!</span>
  <a data-text-id="7402367360841308901" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2070854705" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2070854705" />
    <a title="Maxwell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1381728-maxwell"><img alt="Maxwell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539318702p2/1381728.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2070854705?book_show_action=true">Oct 29, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maxwell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maxwell" href="/user/show/1381728-maxwell">Maxwell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2070854705" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12804257855734422750">At the beginning I thought this was going to be a 5-star read for me. I was immediately sucked in and didn't want to put it down. I loved getting to know the characters; I found the setting and atmosphere very palpable and moody (it mostly takes place on a college campus in the late 1990's); and the Shakespearean elements were fun because I'd studied his work quite a bit in school.<br/><br/>However, as the story went on I found it to become quite predictable, and many of the elements from the beginning st</span>
  <span id="freeText12804257855734422750" style="display:none">At the beginning I thought this was going to be a 5-star read for me. I was immediately sucked in and didn't want to put it down. I loved getting to know the characters; I found the setting and atmosphere very palpable and moody (it mostly takes place on a college campus in the late 1990's); and the Shakespearean elements were fun because I'd studied his work quite a bit in school.<br /><br />However, as the story went on I found it to become quite predictable, and many of the elements from the beginning started to wear on me as a reader. The characters stayed pretty one note throughout. Everything was a bit redundant including the decision by the author to include so much of Shakespeare's text (literally whole passages were copied from his work and it became a drag to read, even when the texts were reflective of the characters' internal monologues—clever at first but the effect wears off). And by 50% of the way through the story I figured out the 'plot twist' which made reading the last half less exciting. <br /><br />All that to say, I would still recommend this book, especially if you are looking for something quick and thrilling to get you out of a reading slump. It's a fun read, even if at times it's a bit melodramatic (I think that's partially the point) and unrealistic. There are a few plot holes and the characters are not the most likeable, but it reads like a CW teen drama and is quite addictive. <b>3.5 stars</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="12804257855734422750" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2569238126" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2569238126" />
    <a title="amy ☂︎" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/61624004-amy"><img alt="amy ☂︎" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1595924086p2/61624004.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2569238126?book_show_action=true">Jan 22, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="amy ☂︎" class="user" itemprop="url" name="amy ☂︎" href="/user/show/61624004-amy">amy ☂︎</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781785656477" href="/book/show/34369803-if-we-were-villains">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61624004-amy?shelf=2020">2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61624004-amy?shelf=lgbtq-rep">lgbtq-rep</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61624004-amy?shelf=favs">favs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61624004-amy?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2569238126" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2135303815932265875"><b>Personally, I believe this book belongs in jail for what it did to me.</b> Coming out of <i>If We Were Villains</i> I feel tainted with the undeniable <i>immorality</i> of it all. I'm left with a sense of wrongness that will probably stick with me for the rest of my life. And yet I'm unhealthily, inexplicably and irreversibly drawn to this book.<br/><br/>There's something so fucking sexy about the intelligence that <i>If We Were Villains</i> posesses. I feel like I became a part of this story, as if I myself just witnessed a murd</span>
  <span id="freeText2135303815932265875" style="display:none"><b>Personally, I believe this book belongs in jail for what it did to me.</b> Coming out of <i>If We Were Villains</i> I feel tainted with the undeniable <i>immorality</i> of it all. I'm left with a sense of wrongness that will probably stick with me for the rest of my life. And yet I'm unhealthily, inexplicably and irreversibly drawn to this book.<br><br>There's something so fucking sexy about the intelligence that <i>If We Were Villains</i> posesses. I feel like I became a part of this story, as if I myself just witnessed a murder that I need to stay quiet about. <b>Like I am the holder of a secret so dark and unholy that I'm never going to be able to say it out loud.</b> There is a sense of intimacy between this book and I that I have not felt towards anything else before. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“Secrets carry weight, like lead.”</i>
</blockquote><br>The characters - <b>a ruthless, conceited band of Shakespeare obsessed assholes</b> - are fascinating on another level. You get to know them so intimately that you'll feel like a part of their little circle by the end of the book. No matter how unethical they are, you cannot hate them. Or maybe you will hate them, but there will always be a quiet voice inside your brain that is going to whisper: <i>“Are you not the same as them, in a way? Would you not have done this, as well?”</i> It's impossible to not at least forgive them for their flaws. The character work in this book is truly one of the most well-executed examples I've ever seen, and it upped my standards to an almost unreachable level. <b>The all-consuming realness of these fictional beings is addicting.</b> And to top it all off, the angsty homoerotic subtext that is present during all of <i>If We Were Villains</i> is [chef's kiss].<br><br><blockquote>
<img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1581249998i/28930721.png" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> </blockquote><br><br>The allure of this book cannot really be explained, but from the aesthetic to the story it is unresistable in its charm. This is <b>Dark Academia</b> at its finest, with morally grey characters that will wrap you around their fingers and play with you like a cat does with a mouse. <i>If We Were Villains</i> is directed towards those that love complicated characters with complicated relationships and a complicated sense of morality, but also towards those that appreciate a fictional figure's <i>palpability</i> above anything else. <br><br><i>M.L. Rio</i> tells a story that will take hold of you entirely, that will not easily let you go once you're done with it. <b>This book will require you to give up not only plenty of hours of sleep but also your deep-rooted sense of what is right.</b> It will force you to think beyond your interpretation of justice and it will make you feel empathy towards characters that have no scrupels. It will alter your perspective.<br><br>In my opinion, this book is unrivaled in terms of thorough character work and gripping story telling and it is from now on unquestioningly considered as one of - if not my favorite - work(s) of fiction. What an entire pleasure to be wrapped up in this deliciously dark, fucked-up story of obsession and vigilantism.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2135303815932265875" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2778443027" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2778443027" />
    <a title="Amy Imogene Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/84702001-amy-imogene-reads"><img alt="Amy Imogene Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548082309p2/84702001.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2778443027?book_show_action=true">Apr 08, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amy Imogene Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amy Imogene Reads" href="/user/show/84702001-amy-imogene-reads">Amy Imogene Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781250095299" href="/book/show/34275217-if-we-were-villains">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/84702001-amy-imogene-reads?shelf=read-in-2019">read-in-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/84702001-amy-imogene-reads?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/84702001-amy-imogene-reads?shelf=mystery-thriller">mystery-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/84702001-amy-imogene-reads?shelf=adult-fiction">adult-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2778443027" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5194473358802187448">5 sonnet-inspiring stars<br/><br/><b>An anti-Shakespeare reader reads a book structured, centered, and deeply versed in Shakespeare....and literally falls head over heels for it?</b> <i>If We Were Villains</i> was amazing. <br/><br/><b>Writing:</b> ★★★★★<br/><b>Structure:</b> ★★★★★<br/><b>Characters:</b> ★★★★★<br/><b>Pacing:</b> ★★★★★<br/><br/><b>Seven senior year college students</b> at an intense fine arts conservatory in Illinois <b>find themselves in their own version of a Shakespearean tragedy</b> as real life begins to blur around the edges of Shakespeare's verse. <b>The hero, the villain, t</b></span>
  <span id="freeText5194473358802187448" style="display:none">5 sonnet-inspiring stars<br /><br /><b>An anti-Shakespeare reader reads a book structured, centered, and deeply versed in Shakespeare....and literally falls head over heels for it?</b> <i>If We Were Villains</i> was amazing. <br /><br /><b>Writing:</b> ★★★★★<br /><b>Structure:</b> ★★★★★<br /><b>Characters:</b> ★★★★★<br /><b>Pacing:</b> ★★★★★<br /><br /><b>Seven senior year college students</b> at an intense fine arts conservatory in Illinois <b>find themselves in their own version of a Shakespearean tragedy</b> as real life begins to blur around the edges of Shakespeare's verse. <b>The hero, the villain, the tyrant, the ingenue, the temptress, the extra.</b> <br /><br /><b>Who plays who, and when, and why?</b> <br /><br /><i>What happens when you become immersed into your role?</i><br /><br />Oliver Marks has just spent 10 years in prison for a murder he may or may not have committed. He's never revealed the truth - until now. Voicing his story to the primary case detective in an off-the-record interview on the site of the crime, <b>Oliver recounts his tragedy in the structure of Shakespeare—in 5 Acts.</b><br /><br /><b>I was hooked by this.</b><br /><br />It is technically Oliver's point of view, but the story unfolds in almost third-person narration as the events of the group's fourth year unravel in atmospheric detail. <b>There is the perfect amount of foreshadowing</b> from Oliver—one liners that allude to future events, etc.—<b>but for the most part, we're living the year alongside the students</b> in real time. <br /><br />One of <i>If We Were Villains</i>'s main selling points is its claustrophobic and almost familial approach to its primary cast of characters. <b>Evoking the unique collegiate mindset of the "found family" friend group in close proximity,</b> the cast of main characters feels disturbingly entwined, and causes deep set emotions to bubble to the surface as the seven work, live, practice, sleep, and act together as one (fractured) unit. <br /><br />I won't go into the seven's individual roles in the book, as part of the fun is immediate internal typecasting and subsequent role shifts that occur naturally. Suffice to say, it's obvious that <b>all is not as it initially appears.</b> <br /><br /><i>If We Were Villains</i> is a one of a kind adventure with a truly unforgettable cast. <b>You'll think about these characters long after you close the book.</b> If you're a fan of the theater, I imagine this is an easy sell. I was not (and still am not) a theater person. But <b><i>If We Were Villains</i> transcends its typecasting</b> and has an appeal for all, not just those who can smell paint on the stage sets. <b>This crime could have happened elsewhere, but it is best shown in its purest habitat—the theater.</b> <br /><br />If I had to pick a negative, <b>the characters' penchant for speaking in snippets of Shakespearean verse was hard to pick up at first...and I'll be the first to admit that occasionally, I skimmed those dialogue chunks.</b> Shakespeare is definitely a living, breathing entity in these characters lives, and <b>in order to dive deep into their story you must dive deep into the Shakespeare they surround themselves with</b>. It's a lot to take in at the beginning, but as you spiral down into the plot it almost (okay, not quite) disappears into the background. <br /><br /><b>This is a strong contender for my favorite fiction (mystery?) of all time.</b> Recommended for anyone who enjoys entangled plot lines with close friend groups, theater-inspired stories, the Bard (of course), and viciously emotionally-motivated crimes.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5194473358802187448" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1942005519" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1942005519" />
    <a title="Diane S ☔" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4159922-diane-s"><img alt="Diane S ☔" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598402138p2/4159922.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1942005519?book_show_action=true">Mar 18, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Diane S ☔" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Diane S ☔" href="/user/show/4159922-diane-s">Diane S ☔</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4159922-diane-s?shelf=lor">lor</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1942005519" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer499399706243707969">4.5. A small elite school, a theater program that is only about Shakespeare, seven friends, seniors, together from the beginning, strong, intense friendships formed. Oliver, our narrator, one of the seven, just released from spending tempers in prison. How did something so special, so promising, go so wrong?<br/><br/>A novel of love, obsession, friendship passion and betrayal. Spending all their on and off time together, this little theater group becomes more important to each other than their real famili</span>
  <span id="freeText499399706243707969" style="display:none">4.5. A small elite school, a theater program that is only about Shakespeare, seven friends, seniors, together from the beginning, strong, intense friendships formed. Oliver, our narrator, one of the seven, just released from spending tempers in prison. How did something so special, so promising, go so wrong?<br /><br />A novel of love, obsession, friendship passion and betrayal. Spending all their on and off time together, this little theater group becomes more important to each other than their real families, than the real world. Shakespeare takes over their lives, the plays they perform, always having to be on, the intense study, rehearsals, they even speak to each other in Shakespearean quotes. The author, and this her first book, does a fantastic job incorporating these quotes, fitting them into the context of the plot, often providing clues and foreshadowing into what has happened. Their obsessions with each other, and Shakespeare lead to dangerous breaks in reality. The plays begin to mimic life and these young people begin to fall apart, deconstruct with horrifying results. We learn so much about these characters, not only from the roles they play but in how they treat each other, how they behave when their loyalty is tested.<br /><br />Not you typical thriller, more character studies but suspenseful nonetheless. It is not necessary to have a full understanding of Shakespeare's plays but necessary I think to be willing to read many quotes and speeches. I loved every minute of it, thought it was brilliantly done was thoroughly captivated by the players and curious to how it would end. A very special, well thought out, and executed debut novel.<br /><br />ARC from BookBrowse.<br />Releases April 7th by Flatiron books.</span>
  <a data-text-id="499399706243707969" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2568265390" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2568265390" />
    <a title="Hillary" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18999155-hillary"><img alt="Hillary" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601752862p2/18999155.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2568265390?book_show_action=true">Apr 01, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hillary" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hillary" href="/user/show/18999155-hillary">Hillary</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781785656477" href="/book/show/34369803-if-we-were-villains">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18999155-hillary?shelf=thriller-horror-mystery">thriller-horror-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18999155-hillary?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18999155-hillary?shelf=dark-academia">dark-academia</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2568265390" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8783780336375320469">*slams hands on table* 5 FUCKING STARS<br/><br/><b>THIS BOOK WRECKED ME<br/>THIS BOOK PLAYED WITH MY FEELINGS<br/>THIS BOOK THRUST ME INTO A NIGHTMARE I WAS HAPPY TO BE PART OF</b><br/><br/><i>
  <blockquote>Actors are by nature volatile—alchemic creatures composed of incendiary elements, emotion and ego and envy. Heat them up, stir them together, and sometimes you get gold. Sometimes disaster.</blockquote>
</i><br/><br/><b>Reading this book was like drowning in syrup. The epitome of bittersweet.</b> I loved it so much it physically hurts. I’m unable to really talk about it witho</span>
  <span id="freeText8783780336375320469" style="display:none">*slams hands on table* 5 FUCKING STARS<br /><br /><b>THIS BOOK WRECKED ME<br />THIS BOOK PLAYED WITH MY FEELINGS<br />THIS BOOK THRUST ME INTO A NIGHTMARE I WAS HAPPY TO BE PART OF</b><br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>Actors are by nature volatile—alchemic creatures composed of incendiary elements, emotion and ego and envy. Heat them up, stir them together, and sometimes you get gold. Sometimes disaster.</blockquote>
</i><br /><br /><b>Reading this book was like drowning in syrup. The epitome of bittersweet.</b> I loved it so much it physically hurts. I’m unable to really talk about it without making it a disservice. I’m going to try here, but know that the only way you can understand what I’m talking about is if you read it. <b>Read the fucking book.</b><br /><br />What was I even doing with my life before I started this book? These characters are part of me now, they’re so important I don’t know what to do with myself anymore. They’re not three-dimensional, they’re so much more than that. <b>I would be reading and I would feel them breathing on my neck. If that’s not powerful I don’t know what is.</b><br />So, guess what? I like books with fucked up characters, weird intricate friendship dynamics and murder, what can I do.<br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>Which of us could say we were more sinned against than sinning? We were so easily manipulated—confusion made a masterpiece of us.</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />I’d never really read dark academy before this book, but I had always looked fondly at the genre, as if I already knew I would love it. Before this one I’d tried a couple of books that classify as dark academia without even knowing, and I wasn’t a real fan. I’m glad this changed because now my life is not the same anymore and all I want to read is campus novels. How weird that it only takes one book to fall into obsession. <b>Though this is not an ordinary book.</b><br /><br />This book made me want to read Shakespeare for the first time in my life since high school? Wow. I’ve had the misfortune of never having the occasion to study his work properly in school or uni, and his language has always intimidated me because I don’t understand it, which means I don’t know where to start. Enter this book. I’d love to reread it when I know more about Shakespeare. I can already see how masterfully the author inserted all the tragedies and its characters in the narrative; every play is there in a precise moment and every actor plays a certain Shakespearean character in a certain moment for a reason. Nothing’s random. <b>Nevertheless, I have a feeling I will never really understand how CLEVER this book is.</b><br /><br />Speaking of which, that foreshadowing, man. <b>The entire narrative is just an ode to obsessive friendship, in both its good and bad connotations.</b> From the beginning you are thrust into the dark world of intimate betrayal, and you can’t help but notice right away. Now that I’m done reading I wonder if there’s even more details I didn’t notice because I didn’t know how the book was going to pan out in the end.<br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>”I think you understand it perfectly. Nothing makes sense to him either. His whole world is falling apart, and once he realizes he can’t stop it or fix it or change it, there’s only one thing left to do.”<br />My eyes adjusted slowly, maddeningly. “What’s that?”<br />His shadow shrugged in the gloom. “Absolve yourself. Blame it on fate.”</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />Oliver was adorable. I was expecting him to be a prick and then he wasn’t. <b>He was the sweetest human being and he must be protected at all costs.</b> The softest moments in the book where his. This book shines a light on him and that’s what he freaking deserves.<br /><b>Oliver and James...let me cry.</b> Not only were they amazing characters, but their dynamics were out of this world. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The DRAMA of their pushing and pulling, they way they care about each other and both understand and don’t understand at what level they do. I was holding my breath the entire time. I had no idea if the book would go that direction, but then it did and I was crying. Thanks for that, btw. We love when a character fakes his own death. You just gave me a HEART ATTACK, James you idiot. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>James looked up, looked right at me. He seemed surprised to see me standing there, though I didn’t know for the life of me why he should be. Was I not always his right-hand man, his lieutenant? Banquo or Benvolio or Oliver—little difference.</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />I predicted most of the ending, but honestly? It made me feel powerful, in a way. And who even CARES. This book was magnificent. <b>It hurt me but I want more.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="8783780336375320469" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2801384916" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2801384916" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2801384916?book_show_action=true">Aug 02, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2019">read-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=dark-academia">dark-academia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2801384916" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10746776048031718169">this book is just <i>that good</i> that I'm having a total overwrought and overwhelmed breakdown. I was just...so so into it. I can't breeeeathe anymore. And I freaking swear; i was about to slam this book so hard across the room and sob in despair and not even rate it -- but the ending. The last fcking sentence. I am a pile of unorganised emotions in a trench coat just...just go. I'll be fine.<br/><br/>[lies. i will never be fine. THIS BOOK. T<i>HIS BOO</i>K]<br/><br/><br/><b>// “Imagine having all your own thoughts and feelings tangle</b></span>
  <span id="freeText10746776048031718169" style="display:none">this book is just <i>that good</i> that I'm having a total overwrought and overwhelmed breakdown. I was just...so so into it. I can't breeeeathe anymore. And I freaking swear; i was about to slam this book so hard across the room and sob in despair and not even rate it -- but the ending. The last fcking sentence. I am a pile of unorganised emotions in a trench coat just...just go. I'll be fine.<br /><br />[lies. i will never be fine. THIS BOOK. T<i>HIS BOO</i>K]<br /><br /><br /><b>// “Imagine having all your own thoughts and feelings tangled up with all the thoughts and feelings of a whole other person. It can be hard, sometimes, to sort out which is which.” </b><br />not only is the book an engaging and compelling and all-consuming story about characters; it also really delves into the greyness of becoming so in-tune with your art, you don't know where it ends and you begin. It's specifically about actors, but I can definitely see how this bleeds into all types of artistry. And oh wow did these kids lose it. So so much. The story is a spiral of losing yourself and facing reality. All seven of them preferred books and plays, art and poetry, to reality and they were very ill equip to handle tragedy that wasn't part of a script. <br /><br />I love books about monstrous things happening to not-monstrous people and then seeing how they react. <br /><br /><br /><b>// “We had, like seven siblings, spent so much time together that we had seen the best and worst of one another and were unimpressed by either.”</b><br />The characters though...<i>the characters</i>. I don't even know what to SAY except vague sobbing. There are 7 of them and I withered inside originally because I'm not good with huge casts (I have the memory of a moth eaten coat) but they all just stood off the page as whole people, complex and mysterious and enigmas, easily and fast. <br /><br />// Oliver narrates; he's the good boy, nice and naive and not quite a good enough actor, but the one who takes up the slack. He is also super gay and super has no idea.<br />// Richard is the leader; the hero, the strongest and therefore the cruellest. he is slowly warping into this horrible person, toxic and frightening<br />// Meredith is the beauty; the one who gets cast as the beautiful woman, the temptress and seductress. she's hates that people don't see past her beautiful body.<br />// Alexander is the resident gay disaster; drug addict to cope and likes to flirt with boys who don't realise they're gay until ~Alexander~ appears. He is "sexually amphibious" which is a beautiful term ok will stan. He is also a creature of dark corners and vulnerabilities.<br />// Filippa, the mystery; she's the background character who gets forgotten and cast to the smallest rolls despite her being quite talented, she's not bold enough. Her life is a mystery and it's never quite unravelled, except she sticks with Oliver through the whole ordeal (despite them not seeming like super close buddies during uni)<br />// Wren was probably the weakest and most delicate; "Richard's cousin" was her main identifier tbh.<br />// James, oh James, I cry; delicate and extraordinarily talented, often the villain caste type and always the one people are drawn to. He and Oliver are roommates ("THEY WERE ONLY ROOMMATES") and their sexual tension is terrible and beautiful. James should be protected at all costs.<br /><br />I loved the characters; they were awful sometimes and self involved others and they were a mess of pretentiousness and vulnerabilities that they hid behind their acting. <br /><br />It is a queer story but it is more about denying that part of you because of fear. (I kind of wish it had been gayer but you know; 10/10 would smack both those boys heads together i cAN'T BELIEVE THEY TREATED EACH OTHER THAT WAY.)<br /><br /><b>// “One sin, I know, another doth provoke; Murder’s as near to lust as flame to smoke.”</b><br />Look I call it: it's a pretentious story. There is SO much Shakespeare in it and do you want to know how much Shakespeare I know??? n o n e. Yet it kind of made me in love with the concept, even if I still don't really understand the core and lines of that style of poetry and plays. It was intoxicating the way the story unravelled, because at times it felt so aesthetic and slow and homey...and it focused on the tight tangle of emotions and how your 20s is such a time of turmoil as well as growth. They're young, about 20-21 I think? And there is jealousy. There are mistakes. There are threats. There is murder. There is brokenness. Guilt.<br /><br />And it begins with Oliver in jail.<br /><br /><br /><b>This book simultaneously inspires and levels me. </b>I wanted <i>more</i> from it in several places, about several things, but mostly I'm just here to be tortured by soft dramatic theatre kid sand their terrible disaster life decisions while half of everyone is extremely suppressing their queerness and the other half is extremely suppressing trauma. I nearly hated it; but then I loved it so fiercely. Also am the ending has left me <i>s c r e a m i n g</i> forevermore.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10746776048031718169" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2585875445" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2585875445" />
    <a title="MaryGrace" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38182573-marygrace"><img alt="MaryGrace" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1504469837p2/38182573.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2585875445?book_show_action=true">Oct 29, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="MaryGrace" class="user" itemprop="url" name="MaryGrace" href="/user/show/38182573-marygrace">MaryGrace</a>

<div id="review_1651964192" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1651964192" />
    <a title="KL (Cat)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5322068-kl-cat"><img alt="KL (Cat)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1416714858p2/5322068.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1651964192?book_show_action=true">Apr 11, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="KL (Cat)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="KL (Cat)" href="/user/show/5322068-kl-cat">KL (Cat)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5322068-kl-cat?shelf=mixed-feelings">mixed-feelings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5322068-kl-cat?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1651964192" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8941900861310152000">Oh god here's to hoping I don't get lynched for this. <br/><br/>Personally, I find making book comparisons in reviews distasteful and frankly insulting to both writers. However there are times when a work comes up with startling similarities before you decide to roll your eyes, and say ok, Cassandra Clare, plagiarizing the Harry Potter series for The Iron Trial is not cool at all (and yes, it's been years but LET ME BE PETTY). <br/><br/>I'm not claiming that IWWV is a copy of The Secret History. Certainly there is </span>
  <span id="freeText8941900861310152000" style="display:none">Oh god here's to hoping I don't get lynched for this. <br /><br />Personally, I find making book comparisons in reviews distasteful and frankly insulting to both writers. However there are times when a work comes up with startling similarities before you decide to roll your eyes, and say ok, Cassandra Clare, plagiarizing the Harry Potter series for The Iron Trial is not cool at all (and yes, it's been years but LET ME BE PETTY). <br /><br />I'm not claiming that IWWV is a copy of The Secret History. Certainly there is more to the novel and Rio brings her own brand of refreshing originality. Nevertheless a core part that makes up the bare-bones skeleton of the world the 7 main characters function in IS a mirror reflection of TSH.<br /><br />A list compiled in my reading notes:<br /><br />1. IWWV: All 7 students are thespians // TSH: All 6 study classics. Both are commonly seen as 'elite' fields that are hard to 'break' into.<br /><br />2. IWWV: Regards each other as "siblings" as repeatedly mentioned by Oliver, (to paraphrase a quote) the closeness of the group meant that there was nothing about each other could any longer affect them // TSH: Richard sees Julian's students (before he joined them) as 'otherworldly' in a way that only they shared - "sic oculos, sic ille manus, sic ore ferebat". <br /><br />3. In both books the characters are specially chosen for their subject; no other students study the same courses as they do. Reinforces exclusivity and especially a 'me vs everyone else' attitude of superiority in the characters. Heavy inter-reliance within the groups. <br /><br />4. Both protagonists (Oliver and Richard) are 'the odd man out'. They are less talented than their peers and both groups know this. Also personally I find them to be painfully bland; perhaps for them to better reflect the brighter &amp; more beautiful like a mirror for the readers. And perhaps to reinforce their longing and precarious position in this elite world that they hunger for, which IMO is a easy way out of explaining their motivations w/ continuing their idiocy (shhh). <br /><br />5. Mostly because both protagonists come from lower-middle class/middle-class (?) backgrounds with families and homes they would like to leave behind.<br /><br />6. Both groups reenacts the course of (Shakespearian vs Greek) tragedy in their lives. <br /><br />7. Both groups had a member that they murdered.<br /><br />8. Said murdered person transforms into an increasingly erratic and uncontrollable character throughout the novel's progression, until they reach a place where both groups consider that murder is the only choice.<br /><br />9. Both groups are taught by mentor(s) that are (at best) unconventional with teaching methods, giving lessons that in turn affect the characters. The university is badly structured with a ridiculous system that allows and in a way encourages these groups to be formed. <br /><br />10. Arguably both books can be split into two parts: what led up to the murder and then focuses on the remaining characters (and their terrible coping methods) immediately afterwards<br /><br />//<br /><br />So! I'll leave this one for you to think about. <br /><br />Similarities aside, this kind of setting that both novels use is unrealistic at best. Personally I find that Donna Tartt makes it work. <br /><br />Her lush prose draws the readers into a place where time is made to seem longer than it actually is. Richard constantly narrates these long stream of consciousness / wallowing / whatever Greek Philosophical Of The Day to the readers. Other aspects build onto this feeling; Julian's lavishly decorated room, and the concepts he discusses (the Divine, beauty, terror), so different and far from 'mainstream' education. Isolation in its all encompassing variety, from Henry's intellectualism to purposely barring themselves from the outside world. Most of the novel takes place where they are alone: their rooms, the library, Julian's classrooms, the ravine, car rides. Whenever they are in a place with other people they are uncomfortable, restless, even to the point of being violent. Snow. The hyper-surrealist quality that saturates everything in the novel helps provide a plausible acceptance for the readers, in regards to the oddity of the characters, and the way they choose to behave in. <br /><br />And as for Rio... I don't know. Mostly her writing is so different from Tartt; If We Were Villains is fast paced, and in turn intriguing. Yet when the scantly detailed prose and lack of character exposition works perfectly for action, it fails to build a satisfying case for the characters that makes them understandable. <br /><br />When everything dramatically falls apart, and the characters choose to behave in their puzzling and overly dramatic ways, I was disenchanted with how their relatively reasonable conduct quickly gives away to unreasonable choices. If you are to be morally ambiguous and make bad decisions; fine. Give me a reason, give me motivations for your actions! To avoid spoilers, and badly paraphrase a mis-remembered quote - there is nothing beautiful or monstrous in being evil for evil's sake. <br /><br />This is not to say that If We Were Villains was not enjoyable to read; rather, it is that I found the first half of the novel that made the latter part captivating - to be quite frustrating. (Also: I loved the ending; it made me go all slow and syrupy inside, warm like molasses.) <br /><br />3.5 stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="8941900861310152000" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2581616696" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2581616696" />
    <a title="JanB " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/260116-janb"><img alt="JanB " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1527313486p2/260116.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2581616696?book_show_action=true">Nov 02, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="JanB " class="user" itemprop="url" name="JanB " href="/user/show/260116-janb">JanB </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/260116-janb?shelf=sarah-s-book-shelves-recommendation">sarah-s-book-shelves-recommendation</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2581616696" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5467124231811803785">3.5 stars, rounded up<br/><br/>I listened to this on a long drive and, despite being well-written, I nearly gave up on it. My initial reaction was I didn’t want to spend another minute with this group of pretentious theater students. Plus I was annoyed by the quotes from Shakespeare. But, since I was driving, I was a captive audience until my next stop.<br/><br/> Soon, things took an interesting turn when one of the students is found dead, and another is accused of the murder. From there, I was fully invested in ho</span>
  <span id="freeText5467124231811803785" style="display:none">3.5 stars, rounded up<br /><br />I listened to this on a long drive and, despite being well-written, I nearly gave up on it. My initial reaction was I didn’t want to spend another minute with this group of pretentious theater students. Plus I was annoyed by the quotes from Shakespeare. But, since I was driving, I was a captive audience until my next stop.<br /><br /> Soon, things took an interesting turn when one of the students is found dead, and another is accused of the murder. From there, I was fully invested in how this story would play out. The person who was accused and convicted is released from prison and the detective who worked the case was never convinced of his guilt. The real story is now told to the detective in flashbacks to the events that took place 10 years prior.<br /><br />I’m not a student of Shakespeare and I still found this to be an addictive read that I enjoyed. Life often imitates art and that point is clearly brought home in this story. None of the characters are likable, so if you require that in your reading, its best to skip this one. I found the dynamics and self-delusions between the friends fascinating. Although I never grew to like this group of students, I did come to understand them, which is a must for me with unlikable characters. It's a interesting character study.<br /><br />Recommended for fans of campus novels and unlikable characters.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5467124231811803785" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2136174899" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2136174899" />
    <a title="lucky little cat" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38160628-lucky-little-cat"><img alt="lucky little cat" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600336662p2/38160628.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2136174899?book_show_action=true">Sep 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="lucky little cat" class="user" itemprop="url" name="lucky little cat" href="/user/show/38160628-lucky-little-cat">lucky little cat</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781250095305" href="/book/show/32076630-if-we-were-villains">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38160628-lucky-little-cat?shelf=disappointing">disappointing</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2136174899" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3213080438917171036">"No, no, no, no."<br/>"Why are people handing this five stars?"<br/>"I don't know, maybe they're all in love with Richard. God knows all the rest of us are." <br/>Really? But then I remembered not <i>everyone</i> was in love with Richard. <br/>"But hasn't anyone noticed it's a lightweight <i>Secret History </i>wannabe, only with annoying theater majors?" <br/>"And perchance with only the most obvious quotes from the Bard?" <br/>"Sh! They'll hear you!" <br/><i>"And </i>you entirely left out the frequent whiffs of <i>Harry Potter</i>-ishness."<br/>"I'm not sure I-</span>
  <span id="freeText3213080438917171036" style="display:none">"No, no, no, no."<br />"Why are people handing this five stars?"<br />"I don't know, maybe they're all in love with Richard. God knows all the rest of us are." <br />Really? But then I remembered not <i>everyone</i> was in love with Richard. <br />"But hasn't anyone noticed it's a lightweight <i>Secret History </i>wannabe, only with annoying theater majors?" <br />"And perchance with only the most obvious quotes from the Bard?" <br />"Sh! They'll hear you!" <br /><i>"And </i>you entirely left out the frequent whiffs of <i>Harry Potter</i>-ishness."<br />"I'm not sure I--" <br />"You know, quirkily decorated exclusive classrooms in creaking historical buildings. 'Pull up a pouf! Have some tea!' Beaky-nosed wise professors with twinkly eyes behind wire frame glasses." <br />"And I say, you've forgotten, that's to say, you've com<i>pletely</i> omitted <i>any</i> mention of the pretty bits of pretentious verbiage."<br />"And people are reading this willingly?" <br />"Seem to be, yes." <br />"Why?" <br />"Well, there's no accounting for taste."<br />"No, there certainly isn't."</span>
  <a data-text-id="3213080438917171036" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
